<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align:left; font-size:smaller">
<center><big><b>Most populous Wyoming City</b></big></center>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Cheyenne</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ʃ/: 'sh' in 'shy'">ʃ</span><span title="/aɪ/: 'i' in 'tide'">aɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><small title="English pronunciation respelling"><i>shy-<b>AN</b></i></small></a> or <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ʃ/: 'sh' in 'shy'">ʃ</span><span title="/aɪ/: 'i' in 'tide'">aɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/ɛ/: 'e' in 'dress'">ɛ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>) is the capital and most populous city of the <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">U.S. state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Wyoming" title="Wyoming">Wyoming</a> and the <a href="/wiki/County_seat" title="County seat">county seat</a> of <a href="/wiki/Laramie_County,_Wyoming" title="Laramie County, Wyoming">Laramie County</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR6_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-GR6-7">[7]</a></sup> It is the principal city of the Cheyenne, Wyoming, <a href="/wiki/Cheyenne_metropolitan_area" title="Cheyenne metropolitan area">Metropolitan Statistical Area</a> which encompasses all of Laramie County. The population was 59,466 at the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 census</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Census_2010_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Census_2010-8">[8]</a></sup> Cheyenne is the northern terminus of the extensive and fast-growing <a href="/wiki/Front_Range_Urban_Corridor" title="Front Range Urban Corridor">Front Range Urban Corridor</a> that stretches from Cheyenne to <a href="/wiki/Pueblo,_Colorado" title="Pueblo, Colorado">Pueblo, Colorado</a>, and has a population of 4,333,742 according to the 2010 United States Census.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FactFinder_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-FactFinder-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Cheyenne is situated on <a href="/wiki/Crow_Creek_(South_Platte_River)" title="Crow Creek (South Platte River)">Crow Creek</a> and Dry Creek. The <a href="/wiki/Laramie_County,_Wyoming" title="Laramie County, Wyoming">Cheyenne, Wyoming Metropolitan Area</a> had a 2010 population of 91,738, making it the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Table_of_United_States_Metropolitan_Statistical_Areas" title="Table of United States Metropolitan Statistical Areas">354th-most populous metropolitan area in the United States</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cheyenne,_Wyoming&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Cheyenne,_Wyoming" title="Timeline of Cheyenne, Wyoming">Timeline of Cheyenne, Wyoming</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%22Cheyenne,_Wyo.,_1876.%22_General_view_of_this_town_on_the_Oregon_Trail_-_NARA_-_531115.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1812" data-file-width="3000" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/%22Cheyenne%2C_Wyo.%2C_1876.%22_General_view_of_this_town_on_the_Oregon_Trail_-_NARA_-_531115.jpg/220px-%22Cheyenne%2C_Wyo.%2C_1876.%22_General_view_of_this_town_on_the_Oregon_Trail_-_NARA_-_531115.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/%22Cheyenne%2C_Wyo.%2C_1876.%22_General_view_of_this_town_on_the_Oregon_Trail_-_NARA_-_531115.jpg/330px-%22Cheyenne%2C_Wyo.%2C_1876.%22_General_view_of_this_town_on_the_Oregon_Trail_-_NARA_-_531115.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/%22Cheyenne%2C_Wyo.%2C_1876.%22_General_view_of_this_town_on_the_Oregon_Trail_-_NARA_-_531115.jpg/440px-%22Cheyenne%2C_Wyo.%2C_1876.%22_General_view_of_this_town_on_the_Oregon_Trail_-_NARA_-_531115.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%22Cheyenne,_Wyo.,_1876.%22_General_view_of_this_town_on_the_Oregon_Trail_-_NARA_-_531115.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cheyenne, 1876</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cheyenne,_Wyoming,_1882.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="461" data-file-width="618" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Cheyenne%2C_Wyoming%2C_1882.jpg/220px-Cheyenne%2C_Wyoming%2C_1882.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Cheyenne%2C_Wyoming%2C_1882.jpg/330px-Cheyenne%2C_Wyoming%2C_1882.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Cheyenne%2C_Wyoming%2C_1882.jpg/440px-Cheyenne%2C_Wyoming%2C_1882.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cheyenne,_Wyoming,_1882.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bird's-eye view of Cheyenne, 1882</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On July 5, 1867, General <a href="/wiki/Grenville_M._Dodge" title="Grenville M. Dodge">Grenville M. Dodge</a> and his survey crew plotted the site now known as Cheyenne in <a href="/wiki/Dakota_Territory" title="Dakota Territory">Dakota Territory</a> (later <a href="/wiki/Wyoming_Territory" title="Wyoming Territory">Wyoming Territory</a>). This site was chosen as the point at which the <a href="/wiki/Union_Pacific_Railroad" title="Union Pacific Railroad">Union Pacific Railroad</a> crossed Crow Creek, a tributary of the <a href="/wiki/South_Platte_River" title="South Platte River">South Platte River</a>. The city was not named by Dodge, as his memoirs state, but rather by friends who accompanied him to the area Dodge called "Crow Creek Crossing".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-city_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-city-10">[10]</a></sup> It was named for the American Indian <a href="/wiki/Cheyenne" title="Cheyenne">Cheyenne</a> nation, one of the most famous and prominent <a href="/wiki/Great_Plains" title="Great Plains">Great Plains</a> tribes closely allied with the <a href="/wiki/Arapaho" title="Arapaho">Arapaho</a>.</p>
<p>The construction of the Union Pacific Railroad brought hopes of prosperity to the region when it reached Cheyenne on November 13, 1867. The population at the time numbered over 4,000, and grew rapidly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-city_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-city-10">[10]</a></sup> This rapid growth earned the city the nickname "Magic City of the Plains".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-city_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-city-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1867, <a href="/wiki/Fort_D.A._Russell_(Wyoming)" title="Fort D.A. Russell (Wyoming)">Fort D. A. Russell</a> was established, three miles (5 km) west of the city. The fort was later renamed <a href="/wiki/Francis_E._Warren_Air_Force_Base" title="Francis E. Warren Air Force Base">Francis E. Warren Air Force Base</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Wyoming_State_Capitol" title="Wyoming State Capitol">Wyoming State Capitol</a> was constructed between 1886 and 1890, with further improvements being completed in 1917.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Wyoming_Stock_Growers_Association" title="Wyoming Stock Growers Association">Wyoming Stock Growers Association</a> met at The Cheyenne Club, which allegedly acted as an interim government for the territory. Many of the WSGA's rules and regulations became state laws.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cheyenne_Regional_Airport" title="Cheyenne Regional Airport">Cheyenne Regional Airport</a> was opened in 1920, initially serving as a stop for <a href="/wiki/Airmail" title="Airmail">airmail</a>. It soon developed into a civil-military airport, serving <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DC-3" title="DC-3">DC-3s</a> and various military craft. During World War II, hundreds of <a href="/wiki/Boeing_B-17_Flying_Fortress" title="Boeing B-17 Flying Fortress">B-17s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Consolidated_B-24_Liberator" title="Consolidated B-24 Liberator">B-24s</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Consolidated_PBY_Catalina" title="Consolidated PBY Catalina">PBYs</a> were outfitted and upgraded at the airfield. Today, it serves a number of military functions, as well as a high-altitude testbed for civilian craft.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-LOC-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_climate">Geography and climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cheyenne,_Wyoming&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography and climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cheyenne,_Wyoming&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cheyenne_Wyoming.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="435" data-file-width="639" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/ce/Cheyenne_Wyoming.jpg/220px-Cheyenne_Wyoming.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/ce/Cheyenne_Wyoming.jpg/330px-Cheyenne_Wyoming.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/ce/Cheyenne_Wyoming.jpg/440px-Cheyenne_Wyoming.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cheyenne_Wyoming.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Late-June 2003 view from the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Lying near the southeast corner of the state, Cheyenne is one of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geographic_centers_of_the_United_States" title="Geographic centers of the United States">least centrally located</a> state capitals in the nation (together with cities such as <a href="/wiki/Carson_City,_Nevada" title="Carson City, Nevada">Carson City, Nevada</a>; <a href="/wiki/Juneau,_Alaska" title="Juneau, Alaska">Juneau, Alaska</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Topeka,_Kansas" title="Topeka, Kansas">Topeka, Kansas</a>).</p>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a>, the city has a total area of 24.63 square miles (63.79 km<sup>2</sup>), of which 24.52 square miles (63.51 km<sup>2</sup>) is land and 0.11 square miles (0.28 km<sup>2</sup>) is water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gazetteer_files_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gazetteer_files-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cheyenne,_Wyoming&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Cheyenne, like most of the rest of Wyoming, has a <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate#Cold_semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">cool semi-arid climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen</a> <i>BSk</i>), and is part of USDA <a href="/wiki/Hardiness_zone" title="Hardiness zone">Hardiness zone</a> 5b, with the suburbs falling in zone 5a.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Winters are cold and moderately long, but relatively dry, with a December average of 28.8 °F (−1.8 °C), highs that fail to breach freezing occur 35 days per year, and lows dip to the 0 °F (−17.8 °C) mark on 9.2 mornings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA-13">[13]</a></sup> However, the cold is often interrupted, with <a href="/wiki/Chinook_wind" title="Chinook wind">chinook winds</a> blowing downslope from the Rockies that can bring warm conditions, bringing the high above 50 °F (10 °C) on twenty days from December to February.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>Snowfall is greatest in March and April, seasonally averaging 60 inches (1,500 mm), historically ranging from 13.1 inches (330 mm) between July 1965 and June 1966 up to 121.5 inches (3,090 mm) between July 1979 and June 1980, yet thick snow cover rarely stays.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_txt_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA_txt-14">[14]</a></sup> Summers are warm, with a high <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diurnal_temperature_range" title="Diurnal temperature range">diurnal temperature range</a>; July averages 69.4 °F (20.8 °C), and highs reach 90 °F (32.2 °C) on an average twelve afternoons annually. Spring and autumn are quick transitions, with the average window for freezing temperatures being September 29 thru May 14, allowing a growing season of 106 days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA-13">[13]</a></sup> Official record temperatures range from −38 °F (−38.9 °C) on January 9, 1875, up to 100 °F (37.8 °C) on June 23, 1954, the last of four occurrences; the record cold daily maximum is −21 °F (−29.4 °C) on January 11, 1963, while, conversely, the record warm daily minimum is 68 °F (20 °C) on July 31, 1960.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_13-3"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA-13">[13]</a></sup> The annual precipitation of 15.9 inches (400 mm) tends to be concentrated from May to August and is low during fall and winter; it has historically ranged from 5.04 inches (128.0 mm) in 1876 to 23.69 inches (602 mm) in 1942.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_13-4"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city averages below 60% daily relative humidity in each month and receives an average 2,980 hours (~67% of the possible total) of sunshine annually. On July 16, 1979 an <a href="/wiki/Fujita_scale" title="Fujita scale">F3</a> <a href="/wiki/Tornado" title="Tornado">tornado</a> struck Cheyenne causing one death and 40 injuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> It was the most destructive tornado in Wyoming history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>

<p>At the 2005–2007 American Community Survey 3-Year Estimates, the city's population was 87.2% White or European American (79.3% non-Hispanic White alone), 12.7% Hispanic or Latino (of any race), 4.5% Black or African American, 2.5% American Indian and Alaska Native, 2.1% Asian and 6.4% from some other race.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> 22.5% of the total population had a <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor's degree">Bachelor's degree</a> or higher.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010_census">2010 census</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cheyenne,_Wyoming&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2010 census">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As of the <a href="/wiki/Census" title="Census">census</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FactFinder_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-FactFinder-3">[3]</a></sup> of 2010, there were 59,467 people, 25,558 households, and 15,270 families residing in the city. The population density was 2,425.2 inhabitants per square mile (936.4/km<sup>2</sup>). There were 27,284 housing units at an average density of 1,112.7 per square mile (429.6/km<sup>2</sup>). The racial makeup of the city was 77.44% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_(U.S._Census)" title="White (U.S. Census)">European American</a>, 2.88% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American_(U.S._Census)" title="African American (U.S. Census)">African American</a>, 0.96% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Native_American_(U.S._Census)" title="Native American (U.S. Census)">Native American</a>, 1.24% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_(U.S._Census)" title="Asian (U.S. Census)">Asian</a>, 0.20% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(U.S._Census)" title="Race (U.S. Census)">Pacific Islander</a>, 4.0% from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(U.S._Census)" title="Race (U.S. Census)">other races</a>, and 3.28% from two or more races. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispanic_(U.S._Census)" title="Hispanic (U.S. Census)">Hispanic</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latino_(U.S._Census)" title="Latino (U.S. Census)">Latino</a> of any race were 14.45% of the population.</p>
<p>There were 25,558 households of which 30.2% had children under the age of 18 living with them, 43.1% were married couples living together, 12.0% had a female householder with no husband present, 4.7% had a male householder with no wife present, and 40.3% were non-families. 33.5% of all households were made up of individuals and 10.6% had someone living alone who was 65 years of age or older. The average household size was 2.29 and the average family size was 2.92.</p>
<p>The median age in the city was 36.5 years. Twenty-four percent of residents were under the age of 18; 9.5% were between the ages of 18 and 24; 26.9% were from 25 to 44; 26.2% were from 45 to 64; and 13.5% were 65 years of age or older. The gender makeup of the city was 49.3% male and 50.7% female.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2000_census">2000 census</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cheyenne,_Wyoming&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2000 census">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As of the census<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR2_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-GR2-5">[5]</a></sup> of 2000, there were 53,011 people, 22,324 households, 14,175 families residing in the city, and 81,607 people residing in the Metropolitan Statistical Area making it the largest city and metropolitan area in the state of Wyoming. The population density was 2,511.4 inhabitants per square mile (969.6/km²). There were 23,782 housing units at an average density of 1,126.7 per square mile (435.0/km²). The racial makeup of the city was 78.1% White or European American, 2.8% Black or African American, 0.8% Native American, 1.1% Asian, 0.1% Pacific Islander, 4.4% from other races, and 2.7% from two or more races. 12.5% of the population were Hispanic or Latino of any race.</p>
<p>There were 22,324 households out of which 30.4% had children under the age of 18 living with them, 49.2% were married couples living together, 10.6% had a female householder with no husband present, and 36.5% were non-families. 31.3% of all households were made up of individuals and 10.6% had someone living alone who was 65 years of age or older. The average household size was 2.33 and the average family size was 2.93.</p>
<p>The city has a wide range of age groups, with 24.9% under the age of 18, 8.8% from 18 to 24, 29.7% from 25 to 44, 22.8% from 45 to 64, and 13.8% 65 years of age or older. The median age was 37 years. For every 100 females there were 95.3 males. For every 100 females age 18 and over, there were 92.7 males.</p>
<p>The median income for a household in the city was $38,856, and the median income for a family was $46,771. Males had a median income of $32,286 versus $24,529 for females. The per capita income for the city was $19,809. About 6.3% of families and 8.8% of the population were below the <a href="/wiki/Poverty_in_the_United_States" title="Poverty in the United States">poverty line</a>, including 11.1% of those under age 18 and 5.8% of those age 65 or over.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cheyenne,_Wyoming&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wyoming_Capitol_Exterior.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="426" data-file-width="600" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Wyoming_Capitol_Exterior.jpg/220px-Wyoming_Capitol_Exterior.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Wyoming_Capitol_Exterior.jpg/330px-Wyoming_Capitol_Exterior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Wyoming_Capitol_Exterior.jpg/440px-Wyoming_Capitol_Exterior.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wyoming_Capitol_Exterior.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Wyoming_State_Capitol" title="Wyoming State Capitol">Wyoming State Capitol</a> in Cheyenne</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cheyenne's government consists of a mayor and a city council. The mayor is elected in a citywide vote. The city council has nine members each of whom are elected from one of three wards. Each ward elects three members. The mayor's office is responsible for managing the various city departments which consist of Street/Alley, Police, Fire, Parks, Fleet Maintenance, Traffic, Sanitation, Downtown Historic District, Weed and Pest, Facilities Maintenance, and Cemetery. The Cheyenne Board of Public Utilities is owned by the city but is semi-autonomous.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cheyenne,_Wyoming&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Public education in the city of Cheyenne is provided by <a href="/wiki/Laramie_County_School_District_Number_1" title="Laramie County School District Number 1">Laramie County School District #1</a>. The district is served by four high schools, <a href="/wiki/Cheyenne_Central_High_School" title="Cheyenne Central High School">Central High</a> on the northwest side, <a href="/wiki/Cheyenne_East_High_School" title="Cheyenne East High School">East High</a> on the east side, <a href="/wiki/Cheyenne_South_High_School" title="Cheyenne South High School">South High</a> on the south side, and Triumph High, also on the south side.</p>
<p>Cheyenne is home to the <a href="/wiki/Laramie_County_Community_College" title="Laramie County Community College">Laramie County Community College</a> (LCCC), one of seven constituent campuses managed by the <a href="/wiki/Wyoming_Department_of_Education" title="Wyoming Department of Education">Wyoming Community College Commission</a>.</p>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text">
<div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cheyenne,_Wyoming&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(June 2015)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><a href="/wiki/Public_sector" title="Public sector">Government</a> is the largest sector of Cheyenne's economy. The state of Wyoming operates a multitude of offices in downtown Cheyenne. Many area residents are employed by or are dependent on the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force" title="United States Air Force">U.S. Air Force</a>, through <a href="/wiki/Francis_E._Warren_Air_Force_Base" title="Francis E. Warren Air Force Base">F.E. Warren Air Force Base</a> to the west of the city, or by the <a href="/wiki/Wyoming_Military_Department" title="Wyoming Military Department">Wyoming National Guard</a>.</p>
<p>Railroads also remain a major economic force for the city, with both the <a href="/wiki/BNSF_Railway" title="BNSF Railway">Burlington Northern Santa Fe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Union_Pacific_Railroad" title="Union Pacific Railroad">Union Pacific</a> employing many residents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>Due much in part to work done by Cheyenne's economic development agency "<a class="external text" href="http://cheyenneleads.org/" rel="nofollow">Cheyenne Leads</a>", successful steps have been taken in recent years to diversify the city's economy. <a href="/wiki/Lowe%27s" title="Lowe's">Lowe's</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wal-Mart" title="Wal-Mart">Wal-Mart</a> both operate distribution centers on the city's outskirts. <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Trading_Post" title="Sierra Trading Post">Sierra Trading Post</a> is headquartered in the city and also operates its distribution and fulfillment centers in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup> In addition, because of the towns cooler summers and abundant electricity supplies (both renewable and non-renewable), Cheyenne has been able to attract a number of data centers including the <a class="external text" href="http://nwsc.ucar.edu/" rel="nofollow">NCAR supercomputing center</a>, along with a <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20131025022547/http://www.microsoft.com/eu/impact-on-society/article/microsoft-building-biogas-powered-data-center-in-wyoming.aspx" rel="nofollow">Microsoft data center</a>, powered by bio gas and <a class="external text" href="http://www.datacenterknowledge.com/archives/2010/12/08/green-house-data-harnesses-wind-power/" rel="nofollow"></a><a href="/wiki/Green_House_Data" title="Green House Data">Green House Data</a>'s data centers powered by wind energy.</p>
<p>On January 2, 2014 <a href="/wiki/Magpul_Industries" title="Magpul Industries">Magpul Industries</a> announced that it was moving its production, distribution, and shipping operations to Cheyenne from <a href="/wiki/Erie,_Colorado" title="Erie, Colorado">Erie, Colorado</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cheyenne's high elevation, coupled with its position on the continent, make it one of the windiest cities in the United States. The abundance of wind makes Cheyenne an opportune place to develop <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wind_energy" title="Wind energy">wind energy</a>. Wind turbines are currently being placed around Laramie County. <a href="/wiki/Laramie_County_Community_College" title="Laramie County Community College">Laramie County Community College</a> is home to a leading wind energy technician program, where students learn to maintain these turbines. The opening of a <a href="/wiki/Vestas" title="Vestas">Vestas</a> wind turbine blade assembly in nearby <a href="/wiki/Weld_County,_Colorado" title="Weld County, Colorado">Weld County, Colorado</a>, as well as other alternative energy manufacturing facilities around <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a>, are transforming the region into a center for alternative energy.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes_Airlines" title="Great Lakes Airlines">Great Lakes Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taco_John%27s" title="Taco John's">Taco John's</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Green_House_Data" title="Green House Data">Green House Data</a> are headquartered in Cheyenne.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cheyenne has one of only three enclosed shopping malls in Wyoming, the <a href="/wiki/Frontier_Mall" title="Frontier Mall">Frontier Mall</a>. The other two are the <a href="/wiki/Eastridge_Mall_(Casper)" title="Eastridge Mall (Casper)">Eastridge Mall</a> in <a href="/wiki/Casper,_Wyoming" title="Casper, Wyoming">Casper</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/White_Mountain_Mall" title="White Mountain Mall">White Mountain Mall</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rock_Springs,_Wyoming" title="Rock Springs, Wyoming">Rock Springs</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks_and_recreation">Parks and recreation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cheyenne,_Wyoming&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Parks and recreation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LionsPark.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/LionsPark.jpg/220px-LionsPark.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/LionsPark.jpg/330px-LionsPark.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/LionsPark.jpg/440px-LionsPark.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LionsPark.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lions Park</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a class="external text" href="http://www.cheyennecity.org/index.aspx?NID=202" rel="nofollow">Cheyenne Parks and Recreation Department</a> operates an Ice and Events center, swimming pool, spray park, skateboard park, two golf courses, <a class="external text" href="http://www.botanic.org/" rel="nofollow">Cheyenne Botanic Gardens</a> (including the <a class="external text" href="http://www.botanic.org/discover/childrens-village/" rel="nofollow">Paul Smith Children's Village</a> at the Gardens), paddle boat rentals in Lions Park (summers only), cemeteries, forestry operations, community house, Youth Activity Center and a miniature golf park. The Cheyenne Parks and Recreation Department also operates a 37-mile (59.5 km) <a class="external text" href="https://www.cheyennecity.org/index.aspx?nid=207" rel="nofollow">Greater Cheyenne Greenway</a> system. The greenway connects parks and neighborhoods of greater Cheyenne. It includes many bridges and underpasses where travelers can avoid high traffic roads and travel above waterways and drainages. In 1996, as a result of the greenway, Cheyenne was named a "Trail Town USA" by the <a href="/wiki/National_Park_Service" title="National Park Service">National Park service</a> and the <a href="/wiki/American_Hiking_Society" title="American Hiking Society">American Hiking Society</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Professional_sports">Professional sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cheyenne,_Wyoming&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Professional sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cheyenne_Warriors" title="Cheyenne Warriors">Cheyenne Warriors</a> were founded as an <a href="/wiki/American_Professional_Football_League" title="American Professional Football League">American Professional Football League</a> team in 2012. After playing a season in the APFL, they announced a move to the <a href="/wiki/Indoor_Football_League" title="Indoor Football League">Indoor Football League</a>. Shortly after the owner of the team died in December 2012, the Warriors announced that they were forming the new Developmental Football League. After playing several games in this new league, the team folded in May 2013.</p>

<li><a href="/wiki/Wyoming_State_Capitol" title="Wyoming State Capitol">Wyoming State Capitol</a></li>

Warren Air Force Base</a>, one of the nation's oldest, continuously active installations (originally U.S. Army <a href="/wiki/Fort_D.A._Russell_(Wyoming)" title="Fort D.A. Russell (Wyoming)">Fort D.A. Russell</a>).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nagle_Warren_Mansion" title="Nagle Warren Mansion">Nagle Warren Mansion</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_Register_of_Historic_Places">National Register of Historic Places</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cheyenne,_Wyoming&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: National Register of Historic Places">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Over fifty different locations in Cheyenne are listed on the <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a>, including:</p>
<div class="thumb tright">

<p>Several districts in the city are also listed, including:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Downtown_Cheyenne_Historic_District" title="Downtown Cheyenne Historic District">Downtown Cheyenne Historic District</a> (1978, with boundary increase in 1980, 1988, 1996. Encompasses 205 acres (0.83 km<sup>2</sup>) and 67 buildings)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lakeview_Historic_District_(Cheyenne,_Wyoming)" title="Lakeview Historic District (Cheyenne, Wyoming)">Lakeview Historic District</a> (1996, 350 acres and 109 buildings)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rainsford_Historic_District" title="Rainsford Historic District">Rainsford Historic District</a> (1984, 1980 acres and 288 buildings)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Capitol_North_Historic_District" title="Capitol North Historic District">Capitol North Historic District</a> (1980, 204 acres and 112 buildings)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fort_D.A._Russell_(Wyoming)" title="Fort D.A. Russell (Wyoming)">Fort David A. Russell</a> (1969, 6,300 acres and 19 buildings)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wyoming_Transportation_Museum" title="Wyoming Transportation Museum">Union Pacific Roundhouse, Turntable and Machine Shop</a> (1992, 113 acres and 2 buildings)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cheyenne_South_Side_Historic_District" title="Cheyenne South Side Historic District">South Side Historic District</a> (2006)</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cheyenne,_Wyoming&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Highways">Highways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cheyenne,_Wyoming&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Highways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<ul>
<li><img alt="" data-file-height="601" data-file-width="601" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/I-25.svg/20px-I-25.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/I-25.svg/30px-I-25.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/I-25.svg/40px-I-25.svg.png 2x" width="20"/> <span class="nowrap"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_25_(Wyoming)" title="Interstate 25 (Wyoming)">I-25</a></span> – North–South Interstate running from <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a> to <a href="/wiki/Wyoming" title="Wyoming">Wyoming</a> intersects I-80 southwest of Cheyenne.</li>
<li><img alt="" data-file-height="601" data-file-width="601" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/I-80.svg/20px-I-80.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/I-80.svg/30px-I-80.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/I-80.svg/40px-I-80.svg.png 2x" width="20"/> <span class="nowrap"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_80_(Wyoming)" title="Interstate 80 (Wyoming)">I-80</a></span> – East-West Interstate running from California to <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a>. Intersects I-25 southwest of Cheyenne.</li>
<li><img alt="" data-file-height="601" data-file-width="751" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/I-180.svg/25px-I-180.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/I-180.svg/38px-I-180.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/I-180.svg/50px-I-180.svg.png 2x" width="25"/> <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Interstate_180_(Wyoming)" title="Interstate 180 (Wyoming)">I-180</a></span> – Bypass Interstate that runs concurrent with US 85 from I-80 to US 30.</li>
<li><img alt="" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/US_30.svg/20px-US_30.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/US_30.svg/30px-US_30.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/US_30.svg/40px-US_30.svg.png 2x" width="20"/> <span class="nowrap"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Route_30_in_Wyoming" title="U.S. Route 30 in Wyoming">US 30</a></span> (<a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Highway" title="Lincoln Highway">Lincoln Highway</a>) – East-West route through Cheyenne</li>
<li><img alt="" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/US_85.svg/20px-US_85.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/US_85.svg/30px-US_85.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/US_85.svg/40px-US_85.svg.png 2x" width="20"/> <span class="nowrap"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Route_85_in_Wyoming" title="U.S. Route 85 in Wyoming">US 85</a></span> (South Greeley Highway, Central Avenue (Southbound), Warren Avenue (Northbound)) – North–South route through Cheyenne</li>
<li><img alt="" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/US_87.svg/20px-US_87.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/US_87.svg/30px-US_87.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/US_87.svg/40px-US_87.svg.png 2x" width="20"/> <span class="nowrap"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Route_87_in_Wyoming" title="U.S. Route 87 in Wyoming">US 87</a></span> – North–South through Cheyenne that <a href="/wiki/Concurrency_(road)" title="Concurrency (road)">runs concurrent</a> with I-25 through Cheyenne</li>
<li><img alt="" data-file-height="393" data-file-width="391" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/WY-210.svg/20px-WY-210.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/WY-210.svg/30px-WY-210.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/WY-210.svg/40px-WY-210.svg.png 2x" width="20"/> <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Wyoming_Highway_210" title="Wyoming Highway 210">WYO 210</a></span> (Happy Jack Road) – East-West route from I-25/US 87 (Exit 10) west out of Cheyenne towards Laramie</li>
<li><img alt="" data-file-height="393" data-file-width="391" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/WY-211.svg/20px-WY-211.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/WY-211.svg/30px-WY-211.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/WY-211.svg/40px-WY-211.svg.png 2x" width="20"/> <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Wyoming_Highway_211" title="Wyoming Highway 211">WYO 211</a></span> (Horsecreek Road) – Runs northwest out of Cheyenne to <a href="/wiki/Horse_Creek,_Wyoming" title="Horse Creek, Wyoming">Horse Creek</a>.</li>
<li><img alt="" data-file-height="393" data-file-width="391" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/WY-212.svg/20px-WY-212.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/WY-212.svg/30px-WY-212.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/WY-212.svg/40px-WY-212.svg.png 2x" width="20"/> <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Wyoming_Highway_212" title="Wyoming Highway 212">WYO 212</a></span> (College Drive, Four Mile Road) – North–South route that forms a beltway around Cheyenne. From I-25 (Exit 7) to <a href="/wiki/Wyoming_Highway_219" title="Wyoming Highway 219">WYO 219</a></li>
<li><img alt="" data-file-height="393" data-file-width="391" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/WY-219.svg/20px-WY-219.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/WY-219.svg/30px-WY-219.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/WY-219.svg/40px-WY-219.svg.png 2x" width="20"/> <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Wyoming_Highway_219" title="Wyoming Highway 219">WYO 219</a></span> (Yellowstone Road) – North–South route from US 85 in Cheyenne near the Cheyenne Airport north out of the city</li>
<li><img alt="" data-file-height="393" data-file-width="391" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/WY-221.svg/20px-WY-221.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/WY-221.svg/30px-WY-221.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/WY-221.svg/40px-WY-221.svg.png 2x" width="20"/> <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Wyoming_Highway_221" title="Wyoming Highway 221">WYO 221</a></span> (Fox Farm Road) – East-west route from US 85 east to <a href="/wiki/Wyoming_Highway_212" title="Wyoming Highway 212">WYO 212</a> in Cheyenne</li>
<li><img alt="" data-file-height="393" data-file-width="391" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/WY-222.svg/20px-WY-222.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/WY-222.svg/30px-WY-222.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/WY-222.svg/40px-WY-222.svg.png 2x" width="20"/> <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Wyoming_Highway_222" title="Wyoming Highway 222">WYO 222</a></span> (Fort Access Road) – North–South route from WYO 225 just southeast of Cheyenne and travels north to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/F.E._Warren_Air_Force_Base" title="F.E. Warren Air Force Base">F.E. Warren Air Force Base</a> and continues on its north route east of the city to WYO 221</li>
<li><img alt="" data-file-height="393" data-file-width="391" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/WY-225.svg/20px-WY-225.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/WY-225.svg/30px-WY-225.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/WY-225.svg/40px-WY-225.svg.png 2x" width="20"/> <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Wyoming_Highway_225" title="Wyoming Highway 225">WYO 225</a></span> (Otto Road) – East-West route from I-80/US 30 southwest of Cheyenne west</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_bus_service">Local bus service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cheyenne,_Wyoming&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Local bus service">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Cheyenne provides local hourly bus service from 6 a.m.–7 p.m. Monday to Friday and 10 a.m.–5 p.m. on Saturday. There is no Sunday service.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">Airports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cheyenne,_Wyoming&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Airports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cheyenne_Regional_Airport" title="Cheyenne Regional Airport">Cheyenne Regional Airport</a> features daily service from <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes_Airlines" title="Great Lakes Airlines">Great Lakes Airlines</a> to Denver.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Railroads">Railroads</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cheyenne,_Wyoming&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Railroads">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Union_Pacific" title="Union Pacific">Union Pacific</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BNSF" title="BNSF">BNSF</a> railroads intersect in Cheyenne. The city is home to a BNSF railyard, as well as the Union Pacific's steam program. UP's <a href="/wiki/Union_Pacific_844" title="Union Pacific 844">844</a>, <a href="/wiki/Union_Pacific_3985" title="Union Pacific 3985">3985</a> and <a href="/wiki/Union_Pacific_4014" title="Union Pacific 4014">4014</a> reside in the steam shop.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-up_steam_shop_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-up_steam_shop-33">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cheyenne_Frontier_Days">Cheyenne Frontier Days</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cheyenne,_Wyoming&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Cheyenne Frontier Days">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bulldogging_a_steer,_Cheyenne_Frontier_Days_cph.3b03105.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1104" data-file-width="1504" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Bulldogging_a_steer%2C_Cheyenne_Frontier_Days_cph.3b03105.jpg/220px-Bulldogging_a_steer%2C_Cheyenne_Frontier_Days_cph.3b03105.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Bulldogging_a_steer%2C_Cheyenne_Frontier_Days_cph.3b03105.jpg/330px-Bulldogging_a_steer%2C_Cheyenne_Frontier_Days_cph.3b03105.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Bulldogging_a_steer%2C_Cheyenne_Frontier_Days_cph.3b03105.jpg/440px-Bulldogging_a_steer%2C_Cheyenne_Frontier_Days_cph.3b03105.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bulldogging_a_steer,_Cheyenne_Frontier_Days_cph.3b03105.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Steer_wrestling" title="Steer wrestling">Bulldogging</a> at <a href="/wiki/Cheyenne_Frontier_Days" title="Cheyenne Frontier Days">Cheyenne Frontier Days</a>, 1910.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cheyenne_Frontier_Days" title="Cheyenne Frontier Days">Cheyenne Frontier Days</a>, which is held over ten days centered around the last full week in July, is the largest outdoor <a href="/wiki/Rodeo" title="Rodeo">rodeo</a> in the US. The events include professional bull riding, calf roping, barrel racing, steer wrestling, team roping, bronc riding, steer roping, bareback riding, and many others. During this week there are many parades and other events. Additionally there is a carnival with numerous rides, games, and shops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup></p>

<li><a href="/wiki/William_T._Kane" title="William T. Kane">William T. Kane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Physicist" title="Physicist">physicist</a> in field of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fiber_optics" title="Fiber optics">fiber optics</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chris_LeDoux" title="Chris LeDoux">Chris LeDoux</a>, rodeo champion and country music legend; graduate of Cheyenne Central High<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Phil_Ligrani" title="Phil Ligrani">Phil Ligrani</a>, Professor of Mechanical and Aerospace Engineering at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alabama_in_Huntsville" title="University of Alabama in Huntsville">University of Alabama in Huntsville</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LaChance_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-LaChance-69">[68]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cynthia_Lummis" title="Cynthia Lummis">Cynthia Lummis</a>, former state treasurer and member of <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">United States House of Representatives</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Edgar_Warner_Mann" title="Edgar Warner Mann">Edgar Warner Mann</a>, Wyoming territorial legislator and lawyer<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Marlin_McKeever" title="Marlin McKeever">Marlin McKeever</a>, defensive end for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_California_Trojans_football" title="Southern California Trojans football">USC</a> and NFL's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Rams_(1946%E2%80%9394)" title="Los Angeles Rams (1946–94)">Los Angeles Rams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Vikings" title="Minnesota Vikings">Minnesota Vikings</a>, <a href="/wiki/Washington_Redskins" title="Washington Redskins">Washington Redskins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Eagles" title="Philadelphia Eagles">Philadelphia Eagles</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mike_McKeever" title="Mike McKeever">Mike McKeever</a>, All-American football player for <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_California" title="University of Southern California">USC</a>, twin of Marlin McKeever<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Joseph_Meyer_(Wyoming_politician)" title="Joseph Meyer (Wyoming politician)">Joseph B. Meyer</a>, Wyoming attorney general and state treasurer<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Nichols" title="Jennifer Nichols">Jennifer Nichols</a>, archer who competed in <a href="/wiki/2004_Summer_Olympics" title="2004 Summer Olympics">2004</a>, <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">2008</a> and <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Brandon_Nimmo" title="Brandon Nimmo">Brandon Nimmo</a>, baseball player for the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Leslie_Osterman" title="Leslie Osterman">Leslie Osterman</a>, member of <a href="/wiki/Kansas_House_of_Representatives" title="Kansas House of Representatives">Kansas House of Representatives</a> from <a href="/wiki/Wichita,_Kansas" title="Wichita, Kansas">Wichita</a>; Cheyenne native<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Charles_E._Richardson" title="Charles E. Richardson">Charles E. Richardson</a>, former newspaper publisher, <a href="/wiki/Rock_Springs_Daily_Rocket-Miner" title="Rock Springs Daily Rocket-Miner">Rock Springs <i>Daily Rocket-Miner</i></a>; retired to Cheyenne until his death in 2009<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tracy_Ringolsby" title="Tracy Ringolsby">Tracy Ringolsby</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sportswriter" title="Sportswriter">sportswriter</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sportscaster" title="Sportscaster">sportscaster</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Robert_Schliske" title="Robert Schliske">Robert Schliske</a>, member of Wyoming House of Representatives, 1971–1975<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Edwin_H._Whitehead" title="Edwin H. Whitehead">Edwin H. Whitehead</a>, former member of the Wyoming House of Representatives and leader of the <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a> forces in Wyoming in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._presidential_election,_1960" title="U.S. presidential election, 1960">1960</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alvin_Wiederspahn" title="Alvin Wiederspahn">Alvin Wiederspahn</a> (1949–2014), Cheyenne lawyer, historical preservationist, rancher, and member of both houses of the Wyoming State Legislature; husband of U.S. Representative Cynthia Lummis<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sister_cities">Sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cheyenne,_Wyoming&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Cheyenne's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sister_cities" title="Sister cities">sister cities</a> are:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bismarck,_North_Dakota" title="Bismarck, North Dakota">Bismarck, North Dakota</a>, United States</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hammam_Sousse" title="Hammam Sousse">Hammam Sousse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lourdes" title="Lourdes">Lourdes</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taichung,_Taiwan" title="Taichung, Taiwan">Taichung, Taiwan</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Voghera" title="Voghera">Voghera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Waimea,_Hawaii_County,_Hawaii" title="Waimea, Hawaii County, Hawaii">Waimea, Hawaii County, Hawaii</a>, United States</li>
</ul>
